  Key Takeaways for Your Call

  The Critical Insight

  Grishi is the gatekeeper. He stated the demo requirement THREE times. Without satisfying him, nothing moves forward. Andrew has the vision, but Grishi has to believe it's feasible.

  The Demo Challenge (Realistic Assessment)

  You acknowledged Databricks is hard to mock up. The briefing provides a tiered approach:

  | Tier         | What                     | Your Effort | Their Value |
  |--------------|--------------------------|-------------|-------------|
  | 1 (Best)     | Their environment access | Low         | Very High   |
  | 2 (Good)     | Sample exports from them | Medium      | High        |
  | 3 (Fallback) | Generic demo             | High        | Medium      |

  Your Strategy: Steer Toward Environment Access

  The pitch is simple: "Mock demos take time that could be spent giving you real value. Give us access to a staging environment or even just 5-10 report exports, and we'll show you what this looks like on YOUR stack. No commitment - just a focused exploration."

  This works because:
  1. It de-risks their evaluation (real results, not theater)
  2. They get immediate value regardless of outcome
  3. It answers Andrew's legacy software feasibility concern
  4. It's faster than you building mocks

  What They Care About Most (In Order)

  1. Agent automation - End-to-end orchestration, not piecemeal Claude usage
  2. SSAS → Databricks connector - Preserving Excel pivot tables
  3. Schema mapping - They've tried Claude, want to eliminate manual intervention
  4. Timeline compression - 3 years → 1.5 years aspiration

  Competitive Reality (Good News)

  Andrew said: "No one has a pre-built package." This means you're not competing against a superior solution - everyone is proposing custom work. Your differentiation is execution capability and infrastructure flexibility ("meet you at your home").

● Now I have the full picture. Let me give you a thorough analysis.

  ---
  Part 1: Holes in the Approach Logic

  Hole 1: The Cognos Integration Claim is Unvalidated

  The claim: "Agents would integrate directly with Cognos, read report definitions programmatically"

  The problem: We haven't validated that Cognos 10.2/10.3 has the APIs needed for this. Andrew explicitly asked:
  "In order for the AI agent to be able to go in and read stuff out of the software or this metadata, either this software has an open SQL server or database, or it has an API endpoint or some sort. Otherwise, your agent... won't be able to connect to that software. Then it's moot point."

  You reassured him that legacy software is "easier to get into," but that's a general statement, not a specific answer about Cognos 10.2's API capabilities.

  The risk: If we get to a POC and discover Cognos 10.2 doesn't expose metadata programmatically, the whole agent approach falls apart. This could be embarrassing.

  What the document should say: Either validate this claim OR acknowledge it needs investigation during the POC phase. Something like: "Integration approach will depend on what programmatic access Cognos provides - report metadata through Content Store database, SDK APIs, or batch export capabilities."

  ---
  Hole 2: Schema Mapping Doesn't Address the Hard Problem

  What Grishi said they already do:
  "We have done this mapping using Claude. The only thing that we're figuring out is that there is a manual intervention, right? We have to feed it the schema and then whatever we are looking for... it's not 100% accurate."

  What we proposed: A 3-phase approach (structural discovery → deterministic mapping → AI mapping)

  The problem: We didn't explain why our approach would be MORE accurate than what they've already tried. Our Phase 1 and 2 are essentially what they're doing manually. Phase 3 is AI - which they're already using.

  The missing piece: What makes our AI phase better? Is it:
  - The orchestrator/judge pattern catching errors?
  - The knowledge graph that persists learnings?
  - The confidence scoring that focuses human review?

  The document mentions these but doesn't connect them to the accuracy problem.

  What's also missing: Grishi mentioned "3 EDW tables → 1 Databricks table" complexity. Our document doesn't address many-to-one or one-to-many transformations at all.

  ---
  Hole 3: The "30% Efficiency" Baseline Creates an Implicit Comparison

  What we know: They've achieved 30% efficiency gain with current Claude approach.

  What we haven't addressed: What improvement should they expect from our approach?

  - If we can't significantly beat 30%, why invest in agent infrastructure?
  - If we're promising 60%, 80%, 90% efficiency gain, we should say so
  - If we don't know yet, we should say that too

  The risk: They might assume we're promising dramatic improvement, and if we deliver marginal gains over their current approach, it's a failure.

  ---
  Hole 4: Timeline Compression is Unaddressed

  Andrew's aspiration:
  "This program can potentially shrink from, I don't know, three years, all the way to maybe a year or a year and a half."

  Our document: Says "scale based on results" but never acknowledges the timeline aspiration.

  The problem: They want to know if 1.5 years is realistic. If it is, say so. If it's not, set expectations. Silence leaves them assuming we agree it's possible.

  ---
  Hole 5: What Happens When Agents Fail?

  The Judge pattern is described as: "Rejects immediately and lives back" [sic - sends back]

  But we don't address:
  - What triggers a retry vs. escalation to human?
  - What if something keeps failing? Infinite loop?
  - How are failures logged and investigated?
  - What's the escape hatch?

  This is a common challenge question for agent architectures. A technical architect like Mahair will likely ask.

  ---
  Hole 6: MCP Connectors Don't Exist for Their Stack

  The claim: MCP provides "stable, reliable interfaces" for tool integration

  The reality: MCP is relatively new. Pre-built MCP servers exist for common tools (GitHub, Slack, databases), but there are almost certainly NO pre-built MCP servers for:
  - IBM Cognos 10.2/10.3
  - IBM DataStage (any version)

  This means we'd need to BUILD custom MCP servers, which is significant work that isn't scoped anywhere in the document.

● ---
  Cognos Integration: Multiple Validated Paths

  Good news - there are several well-documented ways to access Cognos 10.2 programmatically:

  Path 1: IBM Cognos SDK (Java/.NET)

  The https://www.ironsidegroup.com/blog/sdk-bridging-the-gaps/. It can execute "literally all the functionality within the Cognos application" including:
  - Query the Content Store using XPath-like search paths
  - Access report definitions programmatically
  - Retrieve metadata about reports, folders, data sources

  Version note: For 10.2.x, the Java libraries must match the server version, but this is well-documented.

  Path 2: Content Store Database (Direct SQL)

  The Content Store is just a database (SQL Server or Oracle) containing all report definitions, folder hierarchy, and metadata. https://cogknowhow.com/t/cognos-content-store-database-tables-description/906.

  Caveats:
  - IBM warns schema can change between versions
  - Not recommended for production applications
  - But for a one-time migration project, this is perfectly fine

  IBM also provides CMTools.exe (ships with Cognos) for Content Store access.

  Path 3: Report Specifications as XML

  Reports are stored as https://www.ibm.com/support/pages/how-importexport-report-specification-ibm-cognos-analytics that can be exported. The XML contains the full report structure and embedded SQL.

  Path 4: Deployment Export

  Content Administration can export entire folders or the full Content Store as deployment packages.

  ---
  DataStage Integration: Even Easier

  DataStage jobs are literally stored as XML. Multiple extraction options:

  dsjob Command Line

  dsjob -report project job XML
  https://www.datagenx.net/2015/10/dsjob-managing-datastage-jobs-from.html with full job, stage, and link information.

  dsexport Command

  dsexport /JOB=jobname /XML project pathname
  https://geekarticles.blogspot.com/2011/01/exporting-datastage-jobs-from-command.html specifically.

  ---
  Bottom line: Integration is not just possible - it's well-documented with multiple approaches. Legacy software = mature tooling.

  ---
  Now let's discuss Hole 2 (schema mapping accuracy) and Hole 5 (agent architecture detail level).

  Hole 2: Why Is Our Approach Better?

  The gap: They're already using Claude for mapping and getting "not 100% accurate" results with manual intervention. We proposed a 3-phase approach but didn't explain what makes it BETTER.

  Brainstorm - what actually IS different:

  1. Persistent Knowledge Graph
    - Their current approach: Each mapping is independent. Learn something from Report A, it doesn't help with Report B.
    - Our approach: Every mapping feeds a central knowledge graph. Patterns discovered in Finance track carry forward to Merchandising.
    - Why it's better: Accuracy improves over time as the system sees more examples.
  2. Confidence-Based Routing
    - Their current approach: Everything goes to human review.
    - Our approach: High-confidence mappings auto-proceed; low-confidence flagged for human attention.
    - Why it's better: Human effort concentrated on cases that need judgment, not rubber-stamping obvious ones.
  3. Deterministic Foundation First
    - Their current approach: Feed everything to Claude and hope for the best.
    - Our approach: Establish certain mappings BEFORE AI touches it. AI only handles the ambiguous cases.
    - Why it's better: Less surface area for AI error. The 30-40% of "easy" mappings never have a chance to be wrong.
  4. Validation Loop (Judge Pattern)
    - Their current approach: AI output goes directly to human review.
    - Our approach: AI output goes through validation agent first, catches errors before human sees them.
    - Why it's better: Humans see cleaner output; obvious mistakes already filtered.

  How should we phrase this in the document?

  Option A: Lean into the knowledge graph / learning angle
  Option B: Lean into the confidence-based routing / human focus angle
  Option C: Lean into the deterministic foundation angle

  I'd suggest Option C because it directly addresses their complaint ("not 100% accurate"). The message becomes: "We reduce the surface area where AI can be wrong by solving the easy stuff deterministically first."

  ---
  Hole 5: Agent Architecture Detail Level

  You're right that we shouldn't over-explain orchestrator/judge patterns. The document currently has a section called "The Orchestrator and Judge Pattern" that's fairly detailed.

  The question: What level of detail is appropriate?

  Current state: ~150 words explaining orchestrator + judge + validation loop

  Options:

  Option A: Keep but Simplify
  Keep the concept but reduce to ~50 words. Something like:
  "Agent workflows include coordination roles that manage task sequencing and quality validation. This prevents errors from compounding across steps - if something looks wrong, it's caught and corrected before proceeding."

  No need to name "orchestrator" and "judge" specifically.

  Option B: Roll Into Design Philosophy
  Merge it into the "Design Philosophy" section as just one principle among others. The agent specificity and human-in-the-loop points are already there. Could add: "...and quality gates between steps to catch errors early."

  Option C: Cut Entirely
  Remove the section. If they ask about error handling or quality control, you explain it verbally. The document focuses on capabilities, not internal architecture.

  My instinct is Option B - keep the concept but don't make it a standalone section. It's a supporting detail, not a headline capability.

  ---
  Subject: Next Steps: Demo Preparation for Cognos/DataStage Agent POC

  Hi Andrew, Grishi, Mahar, and Sergey,

  Thank you for taking the time to walk us through the full workflow today. That level of detail is exactly what we needed to make the demo directly relevant to your environment.

  What we're building:
  - An MCP connector for Cognos that extracts report metadata and SQL programmatically (eliminating the manual XML downloads from Report Studio)
  - Agent-based SQL conversion from SQL Server syntax to Databricks-compatible SQL
  - If scope allows, a DataStage job conversion that generates YAML config files aligned with your existing Databricks framework

  What we need from your team:
  1. Cognos report XML export from the Finance folder (full export from Report Studio) — Grishi mentioned Vlad can help coordinate this
  2. Target Databricks schema — catalog/table structure so the agent can map to the correct destination
  3. Sample YAML config file from your Databricks framework (so agent output matches your existing format) — Sergey would be best for this
  4. (Optional) DataStage job definition — Mahar mentioned a candidate that was partially converted via Lakehouse

  Once we have these, we can get the demo on the calendar. If any clarification is needed on exactly what to export, we are happy to set up a quick call.

  Looking forward to showing you what the agents can do with your actual artifacts.

  Best,
  Neha

  Subject: Next Steps: Demo Preparation for Cognos/DataStage Agent POC

  Hi Andrew, Gariashi, Maher, and Sergei,

  Thank you for taking the time to walk us through the full workflow today. That level of detail is exactly what we needed to make the demo directly relevant to your environment.

  What we're building:
  - An MCP connector for Cognos that extracts report metadata and SQL programmatically (eliminating the manual XML downloads from Report Studio)
  - Agent-based SQL conversion from SQL Server syntax to Databricks-compatible SQL
  - If scope allows, a DataStage job conversion that generates YAML config files aligned with your existing Databricks framework

  What we need from your team:
  1. Cognos report XML export from the Finance folder (full export from Report Studio) — Monica or Vlad can help coordinate this
  2. Target Databricks schema — catalog/table structure so the agent can map to the correct destination
  3. Sample YAML config file from your Databricks framework (so agent output matches your existing format) — Sergei would be best for this
  4. (Optional) DataStage job definition — Maher mentioned a candidate that was partially converted via Lakehouse

  Once we have these, we can get the demo on the calendar. If any clarification is needed on exactly what to export, we are happy to set up a quick call.

  Looking forward to showing you what the agents can do with your actual artifacts.

  Best,
  Neha

  ---
  Now let me fix all the meeting documentation:

  That's it. Two things.

  DataStage is a separate conversation after we deliver on Cognos.

> Ok, finally, what are we delivering to them? 

● What we're delivering:

  A demo that shows:
  1. We can parse a Cognos report XML and extract the metadata and SQL
  2. We can convert that SQL from SQL Server syntax to Databricks, remapped to their target schema

  That's it. Take a report in, get converted SQL out.

That doesn't necessarily mean that there's raw SQL embedded in the reports. That just shows that we don't know anything about cognitive nodes. You 
need to read the transcript again immediately.

     # Context Discovery
     ## Project Overview
     This is a consulting engagement between BayOne Solutions and Sephora regarding their Enterprise Data Warehouse (EDW) modernization program. Sephora is executing a three-year re-engineering initiative to transition from SQL Server, IBM Cognos, and IBM DataStage to Databricks.
